VI 87:1 Quodam die, cum sponsa consedisset cuidam episcopo et aliis nobilioribus, sensit etc. It is not easy to find a satisfactory solution to this textual problem. The solution put forward in F Gh, i.e. changing ei into ibi, would have been more tempting if the reference were local, i.e. if there hade been a local expression instead of summum caput Ecclesie which, as was pointed out above, refers to the person Clement. A case like I 13:5 Quomodo non demon sedet in eo, qui numquam loquitur sine eo? may prompt another solution: that the archetypal ei is an error for in eo (cf. VI 97:5-7). However, since there are some arguments to be advanced in favour of the archetypal reading, I decided with some hesitation to print it in the edition. 34:23 Deus, qui est cum Patre et Spiritu Sancto creator omnium rerum et <i u- d e x> (addidi; om. codd. Gh) eorum, que facta sunt, etc. The archetypal reading, `creator of all things and of that which has been created', is of course nonsense. A comparison with § 20 of the same chapter, which has a similar text, Deus Pater, qui est cum Filio et Spiritu Sancto creator omnium rerum et iudex eorum, que facta sunt, shows that the word iudex was omitted from the archetype in § 23. As to Deus used of Christ, there is of course no textual problem involved, cf. Rev. I 5:4-5 Deus. .filius Dei, both referring to Christ. It is strange that no copyist, nor the otherwise normally attentive Gh editors, observed the omission of iudex; 34:23 is in this respect comparable to 27:10, discussed above. 
 
 
 
 
 39 35:R anima. . .iam dampnata e x p e te b a tur (o Gh expectabatur ceteri) a nouem demoniis ante principem demoniorum. The distribution of the readings makes it most reasonable to assume that the reading of the archetype was expectabatur. The problem with this reading is that there is no subsequent reference to devils waiting for the soul in question. What is being described in §§ 10-16 is how each of seven devils (two further devils appear in § 26) lays claims to the soul, and six of them round off their claims with the words ideo mea est. These claims are directed to the princeps demoniorum. This means that expetebatur in the heading corresponds better than expectabatur to the following text. There is in the Rev. only one certain parallel to expetere = 'claim', viz. VII 28:21 Alii vero expetunt ab eisdem maledictis maleficis de presciencia futurorum (as to another MS. example of the verb, cf. above, p. 29), and the rarity of the verb may have facilitated some confusion with the palaeographically similar expectare. The o Gh reading, which was probably the result of an intentional correction, is therefore the one I have adopted. The reading expetebatur is supported by the list of headings (see above, p. 22) according to the n MSS. y q, whereas the p MSS. P Y B 0 have expectabatur. 35:35 Sed hoc fossorium nunc deiciunt et assumunt nouum, quia verba mea et institucionem meam vertunt ad alleuiacionem corporis, (verba mea proferunt post corporis add. K verba mea add. ceteri Gh) vt placeant (placeat Gh) hominibus et crescant in diuiciis. The co-ordination of placeant and crescant makes it natural to assume the same subject for these verbs as for the preceding deiciunt, assumunt and vertunt. This means that there is no contextual support in favour of the archetypal repetition of verba mea here; at least I cannot see the point in the emphasized repetition of these particular two words as the object of the preceding vertunt. If the repeated verba mea were authentic, and the subject of placeant, the change of subject would have been remarkable and had most certainly required an explicit pronoun such as ipsi or the like as the subject of crescant.The K reading is an attempt to overcome this textual difficulty, whereas the Gh reading placeat (if not a misprint) is hard to understand. The words verba mea are very likely to have been inserted in the archetype as a mechanical repetition. If so, the error may give us some idea about the length of lines in the exemplar of the archetype, since errors of this kind very easily occur at the beginning or the end of a line. The words verba mea. . .corporis could then correspond to one line in that source, or two lines if the MS. in question was written in two columns. It may be remarked that in the MS. F, written in two columns, the words verba mea happen to stand at the beginning of two lines with one line between (fol. 230ra). 35:37 Secundo commisi eis scopam, qua eicerent terram de fossa, idest vt pauperta- tem et humilitatem diligerent. Sed h e c (q K Gh hoc ceteri) est eis nunc nimis t e- nuis (tenue (2). 
 
 
 
 
 40 The subject of the second sentence must be scopa, and the text recapitulates § 33 Scopa nimis tenuis est. It is therefore necessary to correct the archetypal reading hoc, as was the case in q K Gh. The P2 reading reveals that an error was observed, although the correction is not particularly successful. 39:8 In quo libro sunt septem libri et quilibet habet III (III ex VII corr. Y tres Abe F Gh in marg. q VII r 0 y septem P B Abf K) columpnas. It is quite evident that the archetype had here either septem or VII. It is also evident that the original must have had either tres or ///: in §§ 10-35 there is a description of how each of the seven books in question contains three columns. The error was either caused by mechanical influence from the preceding septem or by VII being mistakenly read as ///. From a palaeographical point of view, the latter explanation is more probable, and therefore I decided to adopt the reading III in the text; this explains the inconsequence with regard to the preceding septem which, in fact, is written as VII only in Ab v q. 39:42 Dyabolus autem respondit: "Non nisi illas solummodo (sc. cogitaciones hominis scio), quas <e x> (o Gh om. ceteri) exteriori operacione hominis et e x (om. K) disposicione eius perpendere possum. The reading of the archetype is characterized by a strange inconcinnity, perpen- dere being constructed first with the ablative and then with ex. The opposite, i.e. ex followed by two co-ordinated ablatives as in the K reading, does not involve anything syntactically remarkable. But the same is true of a repeated preposition — cf., for instance, Rev. I 9:3 ex caritate diuina et ex verbo angeli annunciantis conuenerunt carne — and it would certainly be a miraculous coincidence if a construction like the one in the archetype were chosen in a passage in which the missing ex is followed by a word beginning with ex-. The preposition is thus most likely to have been dropped due to haplography, and though there is some probability that this happened independently in different MSS. — and that it was added not necessarily in the cr hyparchetype but in individual MSS. — I nevertheless took the absence of ex to be an archetypal error. 39:51 et promitto tibi, quod (om. F), si vixero, quod (om. K Gh) volo emendare me etc. The readings in F and K Gh, respectively, are apparently meant to remove the pleonastic use of the conjunction quod, and it is of course legitimate to ask whether the reading of the archetype really reflects the original wording. As a matter of fact, this seems to be so. Pleonastic conjunctions occur in different texts (cf. B. Löfstedt in Vetenskapssocieteten i Lund. Årsbok 1983, p. 30 with lit.), and astonishingly often in the Rev. Cases I have noted are I 52:8 Dic amico tuo, ut patri suo, cuius cor est secundum cor meum, quod hec verba conscripta exponat dili- genter (cf. Undhagen, p. 509), IV 126:91 Ergo si episcopus habuerit istos duos pedes, timendo eciam quod illa, que emendauit, quod forte non sunt bene emendata 
 
 
 
 
 41 etc., V int. 16:24 Ideo non mirum, si hii, qui narracionem euangeliorum ordinauer- unt, quod posuerunt diuersa etc., VI 50:4 Videtur ergo michi, quod, licet ego habeam plures viros, quod, si omnes vocarent me, magis ego currerem etc., VII 7:R dicit, quod, quantumcumque papa et presbiteri sint peccatores, dum tamen non sint heretici, quod ille habet claues Ecclesie etc., Ex. 67:6 dixi tibi. . quod, si. . .vocata fueris de mundo, quod tunc. . .reputaberis monacha in Watzstena and SA 3:12 Edificauit ea voluntate Abraham suo filio habitaculum, antequam conciperetur, vt videlicet quod, quando natus esset, habitaret in eo. To these cases one may add Alphonso's ES 3:15 Congruum enim erat, quod ille castissimus sponsus, qui suam matrem virginem discipulo virgini commendauit, quod suam nouam sponsam eciam regendam virginibus et virtuosis patribus commendaret and 5:28 Ex istis ergo verbis patet manifeste, quod quando dicta domina stabat in visione, sopita gaudio et sopore dulcedinis amoris diuini, alienata a sensibus corporis, vt supra ipsa narrat, quod tunc stabat in extasi etc. Examples outside the Bridgettine corpus are Carpini, Ystoria Mongalorum (ed. Wyngaert), p. 99 Sed hoc debent facere diligenter, ut si contingat aliquos pugnatores redire, quod alii loco eorum succedant, DS X, p. 221 (a. 1373) Rogamus eciam attente, vt, si per dictos nuncios nichil effectum fuerit erga Ruthenos, quod videtur esse pro commodo et salute mercatorum, vt sapienter ad hoc cogitare velitis etc., and Dokumente und Untersuchungen (ed. Nyberg), 2, p. 142 (the text dated to 1441-1450): Item precavenda est quedam mala consuetudo, que vocalibus apponit h, ut ubi debet cantari i vel a vel e, quod tunc apponunt he, videlicet ha ho he vel ha ha hi et huiusmodi. Typical of all these cases except SA 3:12 is the inclusion of a clause between the two conjunctions; in SA 3:12 vt videlicet quod, there is just one word in between, and this makes me suspect that this case constitutes an archetypal error, quod being a dittography of the following quando (as regards the combination vt videlicet, cf. Rev. III 8:5 misit nunciuin suum ad me faciens me voluntatem suam intelligere, ut videlicet fierem mater Dei; cf. also SA 10:9 Congrue quidem decoris arboribus deuota comparantur coniugia, quorum radix est vnio talis duorum cordium, vt scilicet. . .coniungantur etc.). As far as pleonastic use of pronouns is concerned, cf. above, p. 36 (31:41). 46:10 ipse, qui pascit passeres, eciam sustentabit te, q u a m (Fb Gh quem ceteri) redemit sanguine suo. The chapter contains a dialogue between the Virgin Mary and Birgitta, and it is beyond doubt that te in § 10 refers to Birgitta. A feminine form of the relative pronoun is, therefore, as necessary here as, for instance, in § 11 audi me, que sum plena peccatis. The archetypal error was thus for good reasons corrected in Fb Gh. 47:R Qui autem fatigat corpus pro honore Dei, anima eius habebit diuinam dulcedinem et decorabitur, et q u i (que Fb cui Gh ex qui mut. r in ras. K2) detrahitur et non odit detrahentem, ornatur eius anima preciosis vestibus Deo gratis. This passage contains the only case in the Rev. of detrahere in the passive voice. The active voice examples of the verb represent either the absolute construction 
 
 
 
 
 42 (65:31), the construction with de (IV 124:4) or with the dative (65:32). In order to judge whether the archetypal reading qui detrahitur (which is also unanimously handed down in the list of headings, cf. p. 22) is authentic or not, it should first be stressed that the Classical Latin rules for passivization of intransitive verbs are adhered to in the Rev., as appears from some examples: I 32:7 cum venerint opera, euidencius credetur eis (sc. verbis), Ex. 22:1 Qui habet officium principis tempora- lis, tevetur aliquo signo designari, vt ei ab omnibus obediatur (cf. VI 49:1); I 36:3 corpus punitur et partitur anime, VI 13:6 corpus tuum casurum est nec ei parcen- dum est in presenti, and VIII 56:41 regi persuasum fuit cauere ab omnibus peccatis. As far as I can see, also VI 97:3 sequenti die iubetur a Christo confessori redire belongs to this group: although the word-order is a little strange, confessori is an example of iubere with the dative just as, for instance, SA 2:1 vt sibi iussum fuerat and Ex. 37:6 abbatissa vel cui ipsa iusserat (cf. Hofmann-Szantyr, p. 363). That the syntagm iubetur. . .confessori really corresponds to an expected confessor iubetur becomes fully evident from the parallel text in A&P, p. 542: confessor. . .monetur . . .redire. Moreover, I cannot find any parallel case in the Rev. in which these rules of passivization of intransitive verbs are broken. The conclusion must be that it would by no means have been inconsistent with the grammatical rules observed in the Rev., if the original reading in 47:R had been cui detrahitur. This may also have been the case. On the other hand, it cannot of course be taken for granted that Alphonso, the author of the headings (cf. above, p. 12), never deviates from his grammatical norm. The heading of I 44, at least according to the archetype, has this text: Verba creatoris ad sponsam, qualiter nunc despicitur et vituperatur ab hominibus, non attendentes,. . nec curantes etc., and Undhagen, p. 88 f., argues for its authenticity. Nor did Alphonso, the editor of the Rev., observe a case like IV 33:13 Tunc eciam omnis homo discernere et agnoscere poterat ex habitu, quem monachum esse; at any rate, he did not correct it into quis monachus esset. An indication that qui detrahitur is in fact authentic here is the co-ordination with the following non odit detrahentem, of which qui is a necessary subject, whether explicit or understood. It is also possible that the preceding Qui (autem. . .anima eius etc.) made a following qui (...eius anima etc.) natural (cf. below, 47:2). It might even be maintained that a grammatically correct construction Cui detrahitur et qui non odit detrahentem appears a little clumsy and that the idea expressed by the words qui non odit detrahentem is, in fact, more essential in the context than the one contained in cui detrahitur. In the edition I adopt the archetypal reading qui detrahitur, since it is possible to support it with various arguments. The very difficult question of whether and to what extent the original text may have contained grammatical errors will also be dealt with below, p. 50 f. (80:1). 
 
 
 
 
 43 47:2 Nam anima hominis, q u i (scripsi que codd. Gh) audit detraccionem. . ornatur etc. In 47:R qui detrahitur etc., Alphonso is referring to § 2 in the subsequent text, but since he in the heading makes a distinction between man and his soul, it seems most likely that the ch. 47 text that he had at his disposal expressed the corre- sponding distinction; cf. § 1 quicumque . . . animam. This distinction, however, has in 47:2 disappeared in the archetypal reading que, which is corrected in the edition accordingly. The error que was of course easily made, the word anima quite mechanically taken to be the antecedent of the relative. 52:14 Et quia vnus habet minorem intellectum et alius maiorem, sic vniuscuiusque c o n s c i e n cia (Fb K Gh in consciencia corr. r consciencie ceteri) ytor etc. There are a great number of cases of ytor in the Rev., and the construction is with the ablative throughout (apart from a few cases in absolute construction). This fact in combination with the obvious possibility that the preceding genitive vniuscuiusque exerted a mechanical influence is, in my opinion, of greater re- levance than the occasional Late Latin use of utor foliowed by the genitive (cf. Hofmann-Szantyr, p. 83). As regards the comparable case 52:44, see below. 52:36 Tunc autem ista mater mortua alloquebatur filiam vivam dicens: "Audi, 1 a- c er ta (Gh ex lacerata corr. Ab F lacerata ceteri) et venenosa filia mea! The archetype had obviously lacerata here. This word appears now and then in the Rev. and, in particular, in reference to Christ's lacerated body (e.g. I 10:29 quandoque dolor a corde in membra lacerata descendebat et sic mortem prolonga- bat cum amaritudine. Its presence here, however, is difficult to understand. The revelation is about a living woman and her mother and daughter, both dead, and the dead mother addresses her daughter with the words quoted. Since the same woman is in § 77 addressed (by her daughter) with the word scorpio, it seems to be in accordance with the style and manners of this revelation to assume that lacerata in § 36 is an error for lacerta. The word does not otherwise appear in the Rev., and this would have facilitated the error. 52:44 a Deo creata ad celeste gaudium abutebar consciencie m e e (P Y B Ab y F consciencia mea r 0 Fb K Gh) et disposui me ad dolores infernales. The reading consciencie mee, as being the lectio difficilior and represented in all the branches of the stemma codicum, is most likely to have been in the archetype as weil. This of course could be taken to support the reading consciencie in 52:14, but whereas that form could be satisfactorily explained (the influence of the preceding genitive), the situation is more complicated here. Two factors make me hesitant to deviate from the archetypal reading in the present case. One is the difficulty in explaining how the error arose, the other is that the construction with the genitive is, in fact, attested in Medieval Latin texts, as appears from MW, s.v. For these reasons, the genitive is adopted in the edition for this passage, although 
 
 
 
 
 44 this implies that the verb occurs in the Rev. with different constructions (cf. 115:5 Lucifer abusus est voluntate). 52:50 Tibie vero et crura mea sunt quasi baculi spinosi, quia voluntatem meam habui secundum carnalem delectacionem et v o l up ta t e m (Gh voluntatem codd.) meam. The words voluntas and voluptas are notoriously often confused in the MSS. (cf. e.g. 70:7), and in this case it would seem that the second voluntatem was already in the archetype. The presence of the first voluntatem makes a second voluntatem impossible here, which was observed by the Gh editors. A fine parallel is given by § 58 of the same chapter, et sic voluntas et racio sequebantur v o l u p ta t e m (TE Gh volumptatem r voluntatem (3) et delectacionem, where the correct reading seems to have been in the archetype and handed down in n; the situation is identical in § 60. 52:71 Aures quoque mee obturate sunt cum lapidibus duris, quia verba superbie gaudenter intrabant eas et ex ten de b a n t (in extendebantur mut. P2 descendebant G Gh) suauiter in cor etc. The intransitive use of the active extendo, presupposed in the archetypal read- ing, is otherwise unknown to the Rev., in which both the reflextve and the passive constructions appear, apart from the transitive use, e.g. 32:24 non formidat extendere stimulum suum, V int. 12:10 supra mandatum se extendere and VI 33:2 in stipite extendi voluisti. This makes it tempting to follow the corrector in P and substitute extendebantur for the reading of the archetype. I nevertheless decided to accept extendebant in view of the intransitive use of the verb in Eccli. 8,3 multos enim perdidit aurum et argentum et usque ad (ad not in all recensions) cor regum extendit et convertit, with which our passage has some resemblance through the presence of the word cor (cf. Thes. 5:2,1979,33 ff.). 52:91 f. Itaque in corde meo, vbi regnare debuit caritas diuina, ponebatur seruus, idest delectacio et voluntas peccati. (92) Q u e m (Ab F K Gh que ceteri) tunc vestiui, quando omne creatum et temporale conuerti ad voluntatem meam. The context requires a relative referring to seruus in § 91 (cf. § 90 vestire seruum vestibus domini), and que which seems to have been the archetypal reading is then to be corrected to quem, certainly a very trifling alteration from the palaeographic point of view. 52:109 confitebar melius, q u o ( que P quod r) sciui, sed tamen ex timore. This case stands isolated in the Rev., but the archetypal reading quo is neverthe- less to be accepted, since this certainly remarkable use — corresponding to Classical Latin quam optime (potui) — is known from other texts. Johannes of Cologne, general confessor of the Bridgettine monastery of Maihingen, writes in a letter from 1548: Sed necessitate et commissione compulsus, confidens de pietate vestra, 
 
 
 
 
 45 compendiosius quo possum rem et sentenciam indicabo, and later in the same letter: subnixius quo possum rogo et obsecro etc. (Dokumente und Untersuchung- en, ed. Nyberg, 1, pp. 291 and 294). Some examples appear in letters from the Swedish Archbishop Johannes Magnus, 18:5 efficatius quo poterit and 21:1 enixius quo valemus (ed. B. Larsson, forthcoming). The same construction was repeatedly used by Hermann Korner in his Chronica novella (ed. J. Schwalm, Göttingen 1895), pp. 4, 137 f., 289: see B. Löfstedt's article 'Zu H. Korners Chronica novella', forthcoming in ALMA 49,1991. The readings in P and r may be caused either by a lack of knowledge of this usage or the opinion that it was not acceptable. 53:R mensurando se in se i p s is (0 Ab Gh ipsos ceteri) . . .addiscant. . .compati defectibus subditorum. The reading ipsis, represented in only one of the branches of the MS. stemma and not even in all three MSS. of that branch, was not in the archetype, which must have had ipsos. The same is true of the list of headings (cf. p. 22), in which 0 only has ipsis. The text refers to § 5 metiri se ipsum in se ipso (without any variant reading for ipso), and a number of examples confirm that immediately preceded by a reflexive, ipse takes the case of that reflexive, e.g. 121:3 vt. . .sint inutiles sibi ipsis, IV 20:7 mensura teipsam in teipsa, V int. 15:37 vt aliis sit in exemplum et sibi ipsi in coronam, Ex. 58:7 Mensura ergo te in temetipsa; for further cases, both from the Rev. and from other texts, see Rev. VII, p. 75. There is thus reason to believe that the archetypal reading ipsos in 53:R is an error. The passage in 2 Cor. 10,12 ipsi in nobis nosmetipsos metientes, which may have been the ultimate source of the phrase, obviously represents a different syntactic pattern. 54:3 De quo (sc. puteo) omnes bibentes siciebant amplius et lippientes (lippientibus Fb) oculi (Y r Abe Gh oculis Fb oculos Abf ceteri) grauius infirmabantur. The verb lippire appears in two other Rev. passages, IV 58:1 Hic dominus habebat thesaurum preciosum valde, cuius intuitu clarificabantur lippientes oculi, tristes consolabantur, infirmi conualescebant etc. and VIII 2:6 consiliarios,. . quorum oculi sunt ad spiritualia lippientes. Both cases exemplify the adjectival use of the present participle and support the reading oculi in 54:3. I cannot find any case of the construction lippire oculos, which is to be presupposed if the archetype is correct here, either in Medieval or in Classical Latin (cf. Thes. 7:2,1472,52 ff.); the verb is intransitive with either the patient or the eye(s) as the subject. Nor can I find that the accusative of respect (`accusativus Graecus') was ever used in the Rev., and there is thus reason to suspect the authenticity of the reading oculos. If oculi is taken to correspond to the original wording, there is a complication in the fact that the subject of infirmari, contrary to the usage in the Rev., is not the patient but the sick part of the patient's body. This is not a problem as far as Classical Latin goes (cf. Thes. 7:1,1437,45 ff.), and it may be noted that in the passage quoted from IV 58:1, the subject is first oculi and then the sufferers; in 
 
 
 
 
 46 54:3 there is the same change of subject, though in reverse order, if oculi is considered correct. 54:8 Doctores vero gentilium dicebant: "Vtimini c r e a t[u rji s (scripsi creaturis codd. Gh), q u e (quas Gh) videtis, quia ideo mundus creatus est, vt gaudeamus." The reading of the archetype implies a striking grammatical anomaly, which is not very likely to have been in the original text. In order to restoro the authentic wording, one has to alter either the relative or the antecedent. The former solution was chosen by the Gh editors, but cases like 84:5 feruencius diligunt creata quam creatorem and IV 111:6 creata omnia commutare in creatorem indicate that the alternative creatis, que is at least as good. In 84:5, r and y have creaturam instead of creata, which demonstrates how easily this error can arise, as regards a palaeo- graphic explanation of textual corruption of this kind, see the chapter Imaginary abbreviations expanded' of my Palaeography and Textual Criticism, p. 21 ff. In the Rev., creatura and creatum are used side by side, and an instructive example of this is found in SA 2:1 o Maria, creaturarum omnium dignissima, to be compared with § 9 omnes perfectissime amatura eras (sc. Maria) nullumque crea- tum irracionabiliter oditura. 56:11 Viuunt omnino secundum carnem. Iden t r a n s i e t (transibit [-bit in ras.] Fb transeat Gh) ab eis voluptas etc. Apparently, the transmitted reading transiet was not accepted either by Fb or Gh, and taking cases like Rev. V int. 11:7 transibis and VI 113:4 transibit into account, one must of course ask whether the archetypal transiet, known from Ancient Latin (cf. Neue-Wagener, 3, p. 326 ff.), is to be regarded as an authentic form in the present case as well. As a matter of fact, both sorts of future forms appear to be represented in the Rev., and supporting parallels to the transiet in question are found in III 26:20 Nec minimum bonum, quod fit ad honorem Dei, transiet sine remuneracione, 28:14 alioquin transiet ad ciuitatem horroris, IV 112:1 Noli turbari de superbia istorum, que cito transiet and Ex. 98:7 filia tua. . .transiet ad coronam glorie. 57:2 Nec secundum p o ten tes (scripsi parentes codd. Gh) seculi viuebam (sc. Maria) sed cum humilibus humiliter conuersabar. It is not easy to understand the point of the archetypal parentes seculi. Lun&n translates 'enligt världsliga fränders föredöme' (3, p. 126) and the OS version is äptir värlzlicom foräldrom (BU 3, p. 154,5), and both surprisingly suggest that Mary's family was characterized by the opposite of the humble life described in the sed clause. The emendation parentes seculo, i.e. `those who obey the world', would give a somewhat better text, although far from convincing. My suspicion is that parentes is an error for potentes: the phrase potentes seculi was unanimously handed down both in 65:34 and 119:3, and this correction gives the opposite of 
 
 
 
 
 47 humiles, necessary in the context. One may also call attention to Mary's words according to Luc. 1,52, deposuit potentes de sede, et exaltavit humiles. 62:9 Prima quippe hora fuit ab origine mundi vsque ad tempus illud, q u o (v K Gh haud scio an ex quod corr. Fb quod ceteri) per Moysen dabatur lex. Considering the temporal use of quod, dealt with by Hofmann-Szantyr, p. 580 (with further literature, to which D. Norberg, 'Observations sur le latin de saint Victrice de Rouen', Revue des åudes Augustiniennes, 34 [1988], p. 42, should be added), the archetypal reading quod in 62:9 cannot immediately be taken to be wrong. However, the usage actually observed in the Rev. indicates that quo most probably was the original reading. The nominative tempus, followed by quo, appears in II 19:101, III 33:2, VI 40:8, 62:R, 66:47, 77:2, VIII 47:16, 56:98 and Ex.106:5. In two of these cases, there is the variant reading tempus quod (VI 40:8 in P and VI 77:2 in r), proving that the kind of textual corruption I presuppose in 62:9 can actually take place in the MSS. One of the two versions of Ex. 106, known in only one MS., also has tempus quod in § 5, as compared to tempus quo in the other version, which is based on four sources. In other words, the combination tempus quo is very well established in the Rev. Apart from tempus quo, there are also examples of tempus quando (Prol. Math. § 38, and IV 130:11). In only one case, there is in the Rev. a tempus quod unanimously handed down in the MSS., IV 34:4 Adhuc enim est tempus, quod si velit, poterit disrumpere funes etc., but here quod seems to be a consecutive conjunction, the sense being `time—to', and not 'time—when'. The impression that quo must be the correct reading in 62:9 receives strong support, when the examples of tempore quo (or tempore. . .quo) are taken into account (relevant examples of other forms than tempus and tempore do not exist in the Rev.). This combination occurs in I 10:5, III 27:4, IV 7:60, 51:1, 58:8, 70:25, 107:39, 114:22, 129:R, VI 61:3, 89:1, ES 6:30 and 43, Ex. 59:1, RS § 235 (in all three versions), SA 2:2, 13:13 and 18:1. In VI 61:3, P y F Gh have the reading quod, another example of the tendency to replace quo with quod after tempus. This seems to have happened in 62:9, too: an original quo was in the archetype corrupted into quod, maybe due to mechanical influence from the preceding accusative form tempus. 65:22 Sic et Paulus fecit, quia alio tempore necessarior erat et ideo dimissus (Y1 (32 y dimissus est ceteri Gh) per murum in sporta. The addition of est, made independently in different MSS., seems more prob- able here than the independent omission of it, which supports the idea that the archetype did not have est. The ellipsis implied does not lack paralllels in the Rev. text, and the phenomenon has already been dealt with above, p. 31 (13:3). The perfect participle with an elliptical form of esse is the archetypal reading of 115:5 as well, postquam Lucifer abusus est voluntate et mouit eam inordinate, fa c t u s (q F K factus est s Gh) ipse inordinatus et ex mala voluntate malus, and the two cases

V, p. 181. 65:55 quandoque len i o r i b u s (leni- uel leui- codd. leui- Gh) verbis, quandoque s e u e r i o r i b u s (K Gh haud scio an ex seuioribus corr. Fh senioribus B seuioribus ceteri) vsus est (sc. Paulus), qui omnia verba sua et opera habuit ad Dei gloriam et fidei confortacionem. a) It is notoriously difficult to distinguish between n or a u in many MSS., one particular case being 65:55 lenioribus (cf. E. Löfstedt, Coniectanea, p. 73 ff.). As a starting-point in establishing the correct reading here, one may quote Rev. VIII 4:15 caueat (sc. rex) leuitatem verborum et morum in omnibus. According to Birgitta, leuitas verborum is thus to be avoided, and this makes it reasonable to believe that the same attitude held towards leuia verba. Now, the context of 65:55 obviously rules out the possibility of St. Paul using such words as Birgitta disliked. This is in favour of lenioribus in our case, and supporting parallels are easily found in the Rev. In IV 49:18 we read Flectatque (sc. papa) eos forpice, id est verbis lenibus et consilio diuino paternaque caritate, which makes it natural to believe that the original reading of IV 126:73, too, was nec per verba aspera nec per lenia resipiscit; cf. I 32:9 nec lenitas verborum nec austeritas minarum. . .potest eum reuocare. Also in VIII 12:3, lenia verba refers to something recommendable: homo, qui ligatus est ad vxorem per matrimonium, vbi videt periculum suum (=eius), quandoque lenibus verbis vtatur more monitoris, quandoque moderate seuerioribus more doctoris. In my edition of Rev. VII, I chose leuibus and leuioribus in 12:43 and 11:22, respectively, but in view of the parallels quoted I am now convinced that these readings, although there is good MS. support for them, are not authentic: the text should be corrected to lenibus verbis et dulcibus and lenioribus et paucioribus verbis, respectively. b) The archetypal reading (verbis) seuioribus, although lacking parallels, does not seem impossible, but without any doubt the K Gh reading suits the context better. A convincing parallel in favour of this reading is given by Rev. VIII 12:3, quoted above: the antithetically combined lenibus verbis.. .seuerioribus is an excellent counterpart to lenioribus verbis. .se<ue>rioribus in our case. There are no other examples in the Rev. of verba seuera (or seueriora), but cf. IV 134:5 seuerus in verbis. I therefore regard seuioribus as an error in the archetype, the cause of which is easily explained by the abbreviation sign for er having escaped observation. 65:82-84 . . . duplicem mercedem habebit. (83) Primo, quod. . .; secundo, quod . . .Sic erit econtra de illis, qui. . .; erunt quippe... (84) S e c u n d o (scripsi secundo quod codd. Gh) confusio eorum erit sine fine. The words duplicem mercedem are in § 83 explained by two quod clauses. The 
 
 
 
 
 49 negative counterpart (econtra), however, to duplicem mercedem is expressed first by the main clause erunt quippe etc. and then by the clause introduced by (§ 84) Secundo. Parallels to this usage, i.e. an enumerative secundo not preceded by primo, are not difficult to find; see, e.g., Rev. I 54:25 and VI 45:23. The syntactic structure of the passage thus seems to be two subordinate clauses followed by two main clauses, but § 84 quod apparently spoils this structure. I suspect that this quod was erroneously added in the archetype due to mechanical repetition of the preceding secundo, quod (§ 83). It was then handed down in all MSS. and not even observed by the Gh editors. 65:95 Omnis ergo, qui caritatem desiderat in vita activa, sequi debet Martham diligendo proximum, . . ., sed non f o u en do (Ab K Gh facienda Fb fauendo ceteri) vicia eius etc. There is reason to believe that the archetype had fauendo here. The transitive use of fauere is not unknown in Medieval Latin, as appears from SG1, but then it appears in combination with a dative and in the sense of 'grant', `confer'. Occa- sionally, the dative can be understood, DV § 510:2 (ed. Gejrot, p. 204) . . . ut frater. . .transiret. . .ad impetrandum de prelatis et consiliariis regni. . .ut novum locum et apciorem pro construendo monasterio. . .admitterent et faverent. Our case, however, cannot be an example of this usage. In addition, in the three certain cases of fauere in the Rev., the verb is constructed with the dative throughout (II 6:4, Ex. 62:1 and SA 14:3). On the other hand, there are ten cases of fouere, constructed in the expected way with the accusative (one case exemplifying the personal passive, VI 5:11), and although there is no parallel to vicia (or anything similar) as the object, a case like VIII 4:15 comes rather close to our case, eum (sc. regem) fouent (sc. adulatores et assentatores) in peccatis. The material thus seems to support my suspicion that fauendo in 65:95 is an error. 66:9 Quia si sequitur motas suos, s im ile (B Ab F K Gh similes r O similis P Y y Fb) est iumentis. The distribution of the readings suggests that the reading of the archetype was either similis or similes, the reading simile being a correction. This correction is necessary: the subject of the clause must be corpus, since this is the subject not only of the following clause (corpus. . .sit mundum) but also of all the preceding clauses in §§ 6-9 (except the irrpersonal § 8 oportet). 76:5 Insuper scito, quod inhabitator domus huius duplici vicio (Y2 r F K Gh in vicio Y1 iudicio P (32 y q) laborat, scilicet etc. In A&P, there are two parallel texts to this passage, pp. 514 and 629, and since both have duplici vicio laborat, this not only proves that iudicio is an error in 76:5 but it also supports the reading vicio without any preceding in.  50 As far as the preposition in in 76:5 is concerned, it is of course possible that the Rev. recension, as distinguished from the A&P source, included the preposition from the beginning (cf. K) intumuit, vt quasi paritura esset subito etc. The reading of the archetype implies a grammatical anomaly. It was considered incorrect both by K and Gh, and the changes made in these sources certainly restore a more normal syntax. The nominativus absolutus (or pendens), of which the archetypal reading is an example, can basically be regarded as an anacoluthon (cf. Hofmann-Szantyr, p. 143 f.), and it is typical of such constructions that they appear at the beginning of a clause (cf. Eklund, The Present Participle in Latin, p. 168 ff.). The question is then whether a nominativus absolutus can be accepted as authentic in this particular text, but parallels taken from the Rev. indicate that this is actually the case: I 5:5 Tu existens sine principio et sine fine filius Dei, tibi datum est etc., 51:19 Videntes autem tuam delectacionem. . . Et ideo. . .ardebat (the punctu- tation should probably be changed here, et introducing the apodosis), VI 98:8 abbatissa mortua apparens. . .et dixit, VIII 32:9 Venientes autem ambo ad altare meum amicus meus flexo genu. . .dixit. A case with the perfect participle — as in 80:1 — is found in VIII 47:5 Natus (sc. Christus) et veniens in manus meas angeli gauisi sunt. Another argument in favour of the archetypal reading in 80:1 is that the same construction appears in the parallel text in A&P, p. 630. The question of grammatical anomaly and possible deviations from grammatical norms otherwise respected has been dealt with above on p. 41 f. (47:R). I take here the opportunity to point out some other passages in the present edition, the ungrammaticality of which I suspect was characteristic not only of the archetype but of the original text as weil. An example of anacoluthon is furnished by 58:11 Cumque quodam tempore cogitanti michi de passione sua videret me mestissimam respondit michi: "Non credis etc.: here cogitantem (. . .me) would have been more grammatical than cogitanti michi, but the dative was apparently chosen with regard to respondit. Two further examples of anacoluthon are found in ch. 98, §§ 5-6 Non attendens. . .sed. . .recipit and § 8 apparens. . .et dixit (cf. Eklund, op. cit. , p. 172 ff.). A more trivial example of anacoluthon is found in 65:3 (Omnis ergo ille. . .suf- ficit ei). In 10:26, the inserted clause si. . . deliquerit would explain the striking contamination (rogo) vt. . .indulgete. As far as word formation is concerned, 52:67

Apart from 82:1, there are only two cases of debellare in the Rev., V int. 12:22 occultus venire volui ad debellandum dyabolum and Ex. 34:13 mundicia cordis viriliter dyabolum debellabat. Both cases thus exemplify the transitive use of the verb, as compared to the archetypal debellare contra in our case. There is, on the other hand, no certain case at all of rebellare in the Rev. corpus (although it is represented in both branches of the MS. tradition of the Rev. Instructive parallels are, however, found in the Vulgate, in which the verb debellare is always used transitively , e.g. Ier. 50,14 debellate eam, whereas rebellare is weil attested in constructions with contra or adversus (or in absolute function). Particularly instructive are of course cases like Nehem. 2,19 numquid contra regem vos rebellatis? and 4 Reg. 18,7 Rebellavit quoque contra regem Assyriorum. It may be added that the construction debellare contra is unknown to Thes. (5:1,84,30 ff.). From the semantic point of view, too, it is difficult to defend debellare in 82:1. The verb means either 'fight to the end' or `defeat', but the context here requires the meaning 'revolt', `rebel'. The conclusion to be drawn must be that debellare is an error in 82:1. I alone, there are fourteen cases, and a dozen examples are to be found in the present edition, e.g. 6:5, 17:2, 22:21 and 
 
 
 
 
 53 39:64. In all probability, 115:7 also belongs to this group, and si is then to be regarded not only as the archetypal but as the authentic reading as weil. 116:11 Per hanc (sc. dileccionem) m em o r est c o n t i n u e (s continue memor est Gh memor est continuo q F K) mortis sue et iudicii, quo apud me est iudicandus. There are in the Rev. some examples of continuo with the meaning 'immediate- ly' (VII 5:12 si forte tibi aliquis talia persuaserit, tunc continuo custodem, idest racionem, illi facias respondere, RS § 10 Cui continuo vox quedam dicebat, with a similar text in § 290), and there are also quite a lot of cases (almost 50) of continue with the meaning `uninterruptedly'. Two cases contradict this semantic distribution in so far as II 16:14 consulo tibi cogitare duo continuo in corde tuo and 23:39 nisi continuo pensaueris circa te Dei misericordiam et tuam circa eum ingratitudinem, nisi cogitaueris semper ea, que fecisti. . ., non poteris etc. are examples of `uninter- ruptedly' — but both these texts are quoted from Gh, and in both cases good MSS. have the reading continue. In 116:11, the context requires `uninterruptedly', and the archetypal reading — which was probably continuo, handed down in q F K — is then to be corrected accordingly. 117:1 Nullus est tantus peccator nec in tam viii opere positus, <q u o d no n> (scripsi quin Gh om. codd.), si inuocauerit me in adiutorium, ego iuuabo eum. The introductory phrase with tantus and tam seems to require either a consecu- tive or a relative clause, cf. Rev. I 42:4 nullus tam immundus peccator est, si ad me. . .conuertitur. . quod non habebit veniam, III 24:14 nullum peccatum esse tam abhominabile, quod penitencia et voluntate emendandi non deleatur, VI 52:27 nullus tantus peccator est, cui non sum parata occurrere, VII 7:15 numquam tamen est ita malus. . quin semper sit in eo plena auctoritas, 27:31 nullus. . .est tantus et tam magnus peccator, quod ei negetur misericordia mea, si eam pecierit humili et perfecto corde, Ex. 7:1 Nullus est talis ac tantus peccator in mundo,. . quin non statim parata sum venire ad eum (=IV 32:1). There is thus reason to believe that something was erroneously omitted from the archetype in 117:1. The complication with the Gh correction is that quin is in the Rev. normally followed by the subjunctive, and to VII 7:15 quoted above, one may add cases like I 10:28 numquam sic leuiter flagellabatur, quin statim exiret sanguis, 26:28 sic impossibile est tales coniuges spirituales a me separari, quin sim tercius cum eis, Ex. 116:1 brachia mea se continere non possunt, quin pectus meum amplexentur. Moreover, when the mood is indicative, quin is followed by non, as in Ex. 7:1, quoted above. Three further examples of this are found in IV 53:1-3 Non enim est mater, . . quin non statim parata sum iuuare eam...(2) Nec eciam est aliqua vidua, . . quin non statim parata sum perficere voluntatem eius...(3) Non est eciam aliqua vir- go,. . quin non parata sum eam defendere. If the text is to be restored by the addition of a conjunction, it is in better accordance with the actual usage observed in the Rev. to add quod non, cf. I 22:3 nullus homo sic peccator est, si. . .rogauerit, 
 
 
 
 
 54 quod non dimittatur ei peccatum, 42:4 (quoted above), 53:21 Nullus sic indignus, nullus sic malus (sc. est), si vertit se ad me,. . quod non fluunt ora eius lacrimis etc., VI 39:47 Nullus est tam peccator, quod non possit reuerti, . . ., si voluerit. The mood in such quod clauses is thus either indicative or subjunctive. 118:6 opus, quod ab eterno presciui et ostendere e i (s Gh eam q F K) michi placet. See p. 23. 121:1 Obediencia est virtus, qua omnia (s [vide app. crit.] in ras. K2 obediencia F del. q2 om. Gh) imperfecta perficiuntur et omnes negligencie extinguuntur. The most straightforward explanation of the various readings in this case is to assume that the archetype had obediencia (before imperfecta), which was accepted in F but, since it spoils the context, deleted in q and omitted from Gh. There is reason to suspect that obediencia was also the reading of the uncorrected K. The emendation made by K2 is in all respects excellent: it makes omnia imperfecta correspond to the same words in the heading, it creates an appropriate parallel to the following omnes negligencie, and from a palaeographical point of view it implies a very slight change of the transmitted text (omnia written as oia and obediencia as obia, with appurtenant abbreviation strokes). The preceding Obe- diencia may of course also have contributed to this error, which was also corrected in s, albeit in another way than in K. 121:4 Cumque tales considerant defectus suos et retractare volentes priora, statim accedit (Gh attendit q F K excidit s) rubor (robor s) mentis dimittere incepta, et ex pertinacia non audent aggredi saniora. The text deals with excessive fasting. When people realize that they have fasted too much and inconsiderately, they want to correct their former behaviour (as to retractare in this context, cf. VIII 4:11 non erubescat corrigere vel retractare que male acta sunt and Ex. 56:9 paratus errata corrigere et malefacta retractare), but then they are seized with a feeling of shame and, therefore, stubbornly, desist from beginning a sounder life. This is the situation also described in IV 20, which according to its heading is de modo tenendo in abstinenciis incipiendis vel inceptis (cf. incepta in our case): in Birgitta's mind, the Devil's efforts to persuade man to fast more than he can endure lead to a situation in which deficiente robore homo vel continuet male incepta propter ruborem hominum plus quam propter Deum, vel deficiat cicius propter indiscrecionem et infirmitatem (IV 20:6). As far as I can see, the words continuet male incepta propter ruborem hominum must be taken to correspond roughly to the archetypal statim attendit rubor mentis dimittere peccata in 121:4, but then there does not seem to be any satisfactory interpretation of attendit. In the Rev., attendere is used throughout in the sense of `attend to', `strive after', with this meaning the verb would have been understandable in 121:4 if the infinitive had not been dimittere but, for instance, continuare. There is also a syntactic complication involved in attendit. . . dimittere, since normally in the Rev. 
 
 
 
 
 55 attendere is either constructed with an accusative object or followed by ad; there is only one exception to this, viz. Ex. 86:2 homini non. . .attendenti. . .reconciliari (the construction is unknown to Thes. and MW). The reading accedit according to Gh is a very tempting alternative to attendit. One may refer to Rev. V int. 12:7-8 Preuaricato vero mandato accessit statim quoddam erubescibile.. . (8) Accedente itaque erubescencia preuaricacionis mox auc- tus est motus inordinatus etc., a passage in which not only the verb accedere is to be observed but also the adverb statim. The problem with accedit is that a gerund dimittendi governed by rubor would have been the expected form instead of the infinitive. It is, however, not too difficult to find examples of the infinitive for an expected gerund in the Rev. and other contemporary texts, e.g. II 6:11 voluntatem perfectam habuerunt facere voluntatem meam, VI 52:5 da michi auxilium facere, Ex. 7:2 haberet tamen voluntatem nichil curare (but Ex. 17:5 cum firma voluntate vlterius non peccandi), A&P, p. 623 facilitas ire and p. 627 desiderium habuit visitare loca sancta. In Rev. VI 36:2 there is even a change of construction, voluntatem tenendi. . . et. . . viuere . The construction rubor . . . dimittere is thus not without supporting parallels.

 66 LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 7-8 Apparent patrum antiquorum imitatores sed vere sunt in conspectu meo mendaces et defraudatores. Christus prebet audaciam sponse formidanti reprehendendi fiduciali- ter quosdam religiosos in peccatis grauibus persistentes, apud quos ipsa hospitabatur, dicens, quod reprehensio sua non imputabitur ei ad peccatum sed ad meritum, eciam si ipsi ex hoc scandalizentur et indurentur. Christus reuelat hic sponse, quam abhominabilis est coram Deo pres- biter celebrans in peccato mortali et qualiter demones assistunt ei in celebracione misse et de eius futura pena, si non conuertatur. Cap. IX. A B "Ilie presbiter, pro quo tu oras, est quasi forceps, per quam aurum virtutis mee extrahetur. Ipse est quasi ouis degenerans, non curans audire vocem matris. 2 Cum accedit ad altare meum, astant ad latera eius demones, cuius et animam inhabitant, quia ipsa est mortua ante me. 3 Cum imponit sibi superhumerale, demones obumbrant ani- mam eius, vt non cogitet nec intelligat, quam terribile est accedere ad altare meum et quam mundus esse deberet, qui michi mundissimo astare debet. 4 Cum induit se albam, duricia cordis et indeuocione induitur, quia cogitat peccatum suum non esse graue, supplicium eternum futurum non magnum; et quale gaudium est eternum, numquam venit in mente eius. 5 Cum imponit sibi stolam, dyabolus graue iugum imponit collo eius, ita quod delectat eum peccati dulce- do, et sic onerat animam eius, quod non sinit eum ingemiscere vel considerare peccatum suum. 6 Cum imponit sibi manipulum, omnia opera ad Deum fiunt sibi grauia et onerosa et erubescibilia, terrena autem leuia. 7 Cum autem cingit se cingulo, tunc ligatur voluntas eius cum dyabolo, ita quod velit et proponit morari in peccato, et 2-11 cfr J.A.  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 9 69 tunc dissoluitur caritas mea cum eo, quia voluntas eius est ad omne illud, quod dyabolus ei inspirat in mentem, nisi refrenaretur occulto iudicio meo. 8 Cum induit se casulam, tunc perfidia induit eum dyabolus. Quando autem legit Confiteor, demones respondent: 'Mentitus es! Nos sumus testes, quod confessio eius est similis Iude, quia dicit aliud ore et aliud habet in corde.' 9 Cum accedit ad altare, tunc ego auerto faciem meam ab eo. De quocumque autem legit missam, siue de matre mea siue de sanctis, sic michi carum est, ac si meretrix menstruum suum in vase positum offerret alicui nobili ad bibendum aut si aliquis diceret inimico suo: 'Caue tibi! Ego quero dampnum tuum.' 10 Quando vero consecrat corpus meum et dicit: c 'Hoc est corpus meum', tunc fugiunt demones ab eo et corpus remanet quasi truncus, quia anima eius mortua est ante oculos meos. 11 Cum autem corpus meum applicat ad os suum, ex presumpcione illa omnis turba demonum reuertitur ad eum, quia caritatem nullam habet ad me. 12 Ego quippe sic misericors sum, quod, si diceret cum contrito corde et emendacionis proposito: 'Domine, propter tuam passionem et caritatem, quam erga hominem habes, indulge michi peccata mea!', ego susciperem eum, et non reuerterentur demones ad eum. 13 Sed ipse stercus mundi habet in ore, in corde autem vermes sunt scaturientes et ideo non placet ei dulcedo verborum meorum. In corde cogitaciones inutiles comedunt eum, ne cogitet aliquid de me. Propterea numquam accedet ad altare meum. 14 Quid autem est D altare meum nisi illa celestis mensa et gloria in celis, de qua angeli et sancti letantur? 15 Hoc representat altare illud in ecclesia de lapidi- bus, vbi cottidie corpus meum in cruce crucifixum immolatur, sicut olim in lege sacrificia illa representabant, que nunc aguntur in eccle- sia. 16 Quid notat mensa celestis nisi iubilacionem et gaudium?  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 10 71 Mater Dei narrat sponse dignitatem suam et beneficia, que recipiunt ab ea vniuersi. Dicit eciam modum et suffragia, per que anima cuiusdam principis defuncti, pro quo ipsa sponsa orabat, liberari posset de horribili purgatorio; optimum documentum. Cap. X. "Ego sum celi regina, ego mater misericordie, ego iustorum gaudium et aditus peccatorum ad Deum. Nulla eciam est pena in purgatorii igne, que propter me non remisstor erit et leuior ad ferendum, quam careat aliter esset. 2 Nullus est adeo maledictus, qui, quamdiu misericordia mea, quia propter me leuius temptatur a demonibus, quam aliter temptaretur. 3 Nullus ita alienatus est a Deo, nisi omnino fuerit maledictus, qui, si me inuocauerit, non reuertatur ad Deum et habebit misericordiam. 4 Ego enim, quia sum misericors et a filio meo misericordiam consecuta, ostendere tibi volo, quomodo ille amicus tuus defunctus, de quo tu doles, saluari potest de septem plagis, quas tibi filius meus dixit. 5 Primo saluabitur ab igne, quem patitur pro luxuria, si aliquis vellet secundum tres ordines Ecclesie, coniugatorum scilicet et vi- duarum et virginum, vnam feminam tradere nuptui pro anima eius, aliam religioni, terciam, que posset stare in viduitate, quia in luxuria grauiter eciam in matrimonio proprium thorum excedendo peccauit. 6 Secundo, quia in gula tripliciter peccauit, primo laute et vitra mensuram comedendo et bibendo, secundo propter superbiam et ostentacionem plura fercula preparando, tercio nimis diu in mensa sedendo et opus Dei pretermittendo, 7 et ideo, qui voluerit, colligat in honore Dei, qui est trinus et vnus, propter hanc triplicem gulam tres pauperes per vnum annum integrum, et ministret eis talia fercula et eque bona, qualia ipse personaliter comedit, qui colligit eos, 8 nec prius comedat ipse, quam illos tres viderit comedere, vt per hanc modicam expectacionem deleatur illa longa mora, quam amicus tuus X: Il n Gh. optimum documentum cf. Dicta autem missa reficiantur omnes pauperes taliter, quod recedant de conuiuio leti, vt defunctus letetur precibus eorum et pauperes letentur de refeccione. 21 Sexto, quia vsque ad nouissimum quadrantem soluet debita et morabitur in pena, scire debes, quod circa finem suum et in fine voluntatem habuit (licet non ita feruentem, vt deberet) soluendi debita sua. Propter quam voluntatem in statu saluandorum est. 22 Ex quo perpendere potest homo, quanta est misericordia filii mei, qui pro tam modico dat requiem. Et nisi illam voluntatem habuisset, ipse sine fine dampnatus fuisset. 23 Ideo debent parentes sui, qui in honis suis successerunt, habere voluntatem soluendi et soluere debi- ta sua, quibuscumque nouerint debere. Et quibus soluunt debitum suum, rogent eos humiliter, vt indulgeant anime eius, si dampnum 'ex longa expectacione incurrerint. Alioquin dicti parentes defuncti pec- catum illius portabunt, si non soluerint. 24 Deinde cuilibet monaste- rio in regno mittat oblacionem, qualem voluerit, et faciat dici vnam missam in conuentu publice, et antequam incipiatur missa, rogetur pro anima eius, vt placatus sit ei Deus. 25 Postea dicatur vna missa pro defunctis in qualibet ecclesia parrochiali, in qua bona sua habuit. Declaracio. 36 Hic fuit nobilis et misericors. Hic mortuus apparuit domine Birgitte dicens: "Nichil me tantum eleuat a tribulacionibus meis sicut oracio iustorum et sacramentum altaris. 37 Verum quia iudex fui et iudicia mea commisi huis, qui minus diligebant iusticiam, ideo adhuc detineor in exilio. Sed cicius liberarer, si hii, qui mei deberent esse et fuerunt, essent ad meam salutem miciores." Item de eodem in isto libro XXI. capitulo. Mater Dei monet sponsam, quod semper recordetur de dolorosa passione Christi, quia in illa hora passionis Christi omnia quasi conturbabantur, scilicet deitas et humanitas et ipsa mater eius, angeli et omnia elementa et omnes anime viuencium et mortuorum et eciam demones. Cap. XI. Mater Dei loquitur ad sponsam dicens: "In morte filii mei omnia conturbabantur. 2 Nam deitas, que Filium tradidit in mortem et numquam ab eo separabatur, nec in morte, in illa horula mortis tamquam compaciens videbatur, licet nullum dolorem vel penam deitas pati possit, quia impassibilis et immutabilis est. 3 Filius ipse paciebatur dolorem in omnibus membris et eciam in corde, qui tamen secundum deitatem erat immortalis.  76 B LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 11 immortalis erat, paciebatur, quia exiuit de corpore. 4 Congregati angeli eciam quasi turbati videbantur, cum viderent Deum in huma- nitate pati in terra. Sed quomodo turbari possunt angeli, qui immor- tales sunt? 5 Vtique, sicut iustus, cum videret amicum suum pati aliqua, de quibus consequeretur maximam gloriam, et gauderet qui- dem de gloria eius adipiscenda sed tamen propter passionem quasi quodammodo contristaretur, 6 sic angeli quasi contristabantur de pena eius, cum tamen sunt impassibiles, sed gaudebant de gloria eius futura et vtilitate ex passione eius ventura. 7 Omnia quoque elemen- ta turbabantur: et sol et luna dimiserunt splendorem suum, terra tremuit, lapides scindebantur et sepulchra aperiebantur in hora mor- tis filii mei. 8 Omnes gentiles turbabantur, vbicumque erant, quia in corde eorum venit quasi quedam punctura doloris, licet nescierunt, vnde esset. Tribulabatur eciam cor crucifigencium eum in illa hora sed non ad gloriam eorum. 9 Adhuc eciam immundi spiritus turba- bantur in illa hora et quasi in vnum congregati turbabantur. Illi autem, qui erant in sinu Abrahe, multum turbabantur, in tantum quod mallent in eternum esse in inferno quam talem penam in suo Domino videre. 10 Ego autem, que tunc eidem filio meo astabam, virgo et mater eius, qualem dolorem tunc paciebar, nullus potest considerare. 11 Ideo, filia mea, recordare passionem filii mei, fuge instabilitatem mundi, qui non est nisi quidam visus et flos cito arescens." lapides scindebantur et sepulchra aperiebantur cfr Matth. 7 terra tremuit Ps. 75,9 10 astabam cfr loh. 19,25 9 in sinu Abrahe cfr Luc. 16,23 27,51 sqq. viderent (3 F turbari Gh 4 eciam q2 om.  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 12 77 Mater Dei dicit, quod ipsa similis est alueario apum, quia illa benedic- ta apis celestis, scilicet filius Dei, repleuit eam melle dulcissimo, quando descendit in vtero eius, sic copiose, quod ex illa dulcedine omnis sapor venenatus a nobis sublatus est. Cap. XII. Beata virgo loquebatur ad sponsam dicens: "Sponsa filii mei, tu salutabas me et comparabas alueario apum. Ego certe fui [apis]. Nam corpus meum fuit quasi lignum solum in vtero matris, ante- quam anima coniungeretur. 2 Fuit eciam corpus meum post mortem meam quasi lignum separata anima, vsquequo meam animam Deus cum corpore ad deitatem sublimauit. 3 Hoc lignum factum est aluea- rium, quando illa benedicta apis, filius Dei, traxit se de celis et Deus viuus descendit in corpus meum. 4 In me denique fuit quidam dulcissimus et subtilissimus fauus, qui preparatus erat omnibus mo- dis et accessionsbus ad suscipiendum dulcissimum mel gracie Spiritus Sancti. 5 Hic fauus tunc impletus est, quando filius Dei venit in me cum potencia et caritate et honestate. Venit cum potencia, quia Dominus et Deus meus erat. 6 Venit cum caritate, quia pro caritate, quam ad animas habuit, carnem assumpsit et crucem. Venit cum honestate, quia omne peccatum Ade segregatum fuit a me. Vnde filius Dei honestissimus honestissimam carnem assumpsit. 7 Sed sicut apis habet aculeum, cum quo tamen non pungit nisi inuita, sic filius meus habet seueritatem iusticie, quam tamen non exercet, nisi quan- do est a peccatis prouocatus. 8 Huic api male retributum est. Nam pro potencia traditus est in manus iniquorum, pro caritate datus est in manus crudelium, pro honestate nudatus est et immisericorditer flagellatus. 9 Benedicta ergo sit apis illa, que de ligno meo fecit sibi apiarium et impleuit eum melle suo sic copiose, vt de dulcedine michi data sapor ille venenatus de ore omnium auferetur."  78 L1BRI SEXTI CAP. 13 Christus monet sponsam, quod omne tempus dispenset secundum voluntatem Dei nec aliquid faciat, nisi que Deo placere credat, et quod semper habeat voluntatem standi in seruicio Dei et mentem iugiter eleuet ad celestia, corpus quoque suum fatiget in presenti taliter, quod possit resurgere ad futuram gloriam. Cap. XIII. A B Loquitur Filius ad sponsam: "Tu debes habere tria: primo non ire nisi ad voluntatem meam, secundo non sedere nisi ad honorem meum, tercio non stare debes nisi ad vtilitatem sponsi. 2 Tunc autem vadis ad voluntatem meam, quando omne tempus tuum dispensas ad voluntatem meam, quando non comedis nec dormis nec aliud quid- quam facis, nisi sicut michi placere intelligis. 3 Stas autem firmiter, cum voluntatem habes stare in seruicio meo, sedes vero tunc, quan- do mentem tuam iugiter ad celestia eleuas considerando, qualis gloria sanctorum et vita sempiterna. 4 Hiis ergo tribus alia tria debes addere. Primo debes disposita esse sicut virgo desponsatura, que cogitat sic apud se: 5 'Omnia, que possum, de honis patris mei, que casura sunt, congregabo michi ad sponsum meum, cum quo debeo esse in necessitate et aduersitate.' Sic et tu facere debes, quia quasi pater tuus corpus tuum est. 6 Ab hoc enim omnem laborem, quem poteris, in pauperes et alia bona exigere debes, vt mecum quasi cum sponso letari possis. Quia corpus tuum casurum est nec ei parcen- dum est in presenti, vt in futuro resurgat ad meliorem vitam. 7 Secundo cogita tecum, sicut bona yxor cogitat secum: 'Si vir mens diligit me, cur debeo sollicitari? Si pacificus est michi, quem tunc habeo timere? Ideo, ne irascatur michi, exhibebo ei omnem hono- rem et stabo semper ad voluntatem eius.' 8 Tercio cogita tecum, quod sponsus tuus est eternus et ditissimus, cum quo habebis hono- rem perpetuum et diuicias eternas. Et ideo noli diligere casura, vt optinere possis eternaliter permansura."  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 14 79 Christus declarat sponse, qualiter ipse fecerat per angelum eam more paruuli enutriri in vita spirituali et virtutibus, et iterum recommendat eam angelo. Narrat eciam, qualiter sancta decepcione deduxit eam de mundo ad quietis portum, et precipit, quod omnes temptaciones reuelet suis patribus spiritualibus et habebit finem perfectum. Cap. XIV. Quidam angelorum loquebatur ad Deum dicens: "Laus tibi sit, Domine mi, ab omni exercitu tuo pro omni dileccione tua! Tu assignasti custodie mee hanc sponsam hic stantem; ecce ipsam tibi iterum reassigno. 2 Ego enim alliciebam eam ad te quasi paruulam, primo dando pomum; deinde comesto pomo dixi ei: 'Sequere me, filia, amplius et dabo tibi vinum dulcissimum. Quia in pomo non est nisi modicus sapor, in vino vero dulcedo et animi exultacio.' 3 Gustato autem vino dixi iterum ad eam: 'Procede adhuc viterius et dispono tibi quod est in eternum, in quo est omne bonum."' 4 Hiis dictis dixit Dominus ad sponsam: "Verum est, quod seruus meus te audiente loquebatur. Ipse vtique quasi per pomum alliciebat te tunc ad me, quando cogitabas tecum omnia esse a me, que habebas, et regraciabaris michi soli pro eis. 5 Quia sicut in pomo non est nisi sapor quidam et modica sacietas, sic tunc temporis non multum sapiebat tibi caritas mea, nisi quasi quidam sapor cognicionis Dei esset in corde tuo. 6 Tunc vero viterius processisti, quando cogitasti tecum sic: 'Gloria Dei est eterna et mundi leticia nimis breuis et in fine mundi nimis inutilis. Quid michi prodest, quod ista temporalia sic diligam?' 7 Ex tali cogitacione cepisti viriliter absti- nere a delectacionibus mundi et facere bona, que poteras, in nomine meo. Et tunc quasi desiderio affecta vini amplius me sitisti. 8 Deinde cum cogitasti me esse omnipotentem Dominum, a quo est omne bonum, et reliquisti voluntatem tuam faciendo meam, tunc iure facta es mea et consensi in te et feci te esse meam."  80 LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 14 9 Quo dicto dixit Dominus ad angelum: "Serue meus, tu diues es in me, honor tuus est eternus, ignis caritatis tue inextinguibilis, virtus tua indeficiens. 10 Tu assignasti michi sponsam meam, sed volo, quod custodias eam adhuc, donec venerit ad etatem. Custodi eam, ne dyabolus aliqua incaute sibi obiciat! 11 Prouide sibi vestes virtu- tum, vestes tocius pulchritudinis! Ciba eam verbis meis, que sunt tamquam carnes recentes, quibus sanguis melioratur, caro infirma c conualescit et delectacio bona in anima excitatur. 12 Ego enim feci isti, sicut aliquis solet facere amico suo, quem pro caritate et bono suo captivat. Dicit enim ei captivans: 'Amice, ingredere in domum meam et vide ibi, que aguntur, que tibi sunt facienda.' 13 Quo ingrediente non ostendit ei captivator vilissimos serpentes et ferocis- simos leones, qui habitant in domo, ne terreatur amicus, sed in consolacionem amici facit serpentes videri, quasi sint oues mansue- tissime, leones quasi oues pulchras, dicens amico suo: 14 'Amice, scito, quod diligo te et pro bono tuo captivaui te. Ideo, quecumque videris, dic amicis meis; ipsi enim custodiunt te et consolabuntur te ita, quod melius placebit tibi captiuitas mea quam propria libertas tua.' Sic, filia dilecta, simili modo ego feci tibi. 15 Ego enim quasi captivaui te, cum a delectacione tua reuocaui te ad amorem meum, cum a mundi periculis vocaui in hunc quietis portum, in quo, quos tu putas esse virgines per continenciam, veraciter leones sunt per mali- ciam, quos tu credis oues per diuinam contemplacionem, hii quasi serpentes gradiuntur in ventre gule et cupiditatis. 16 Ideo, quecum- que videris et audieris, non ad alium referas sed ad amicos meos, qui te custodiunt et instruunt. 17 Quia Spiritus, qui te duxit in portum, ipse te ducet ad patriam, et qui te adduxit ad principium bonum, ipse te ducet ad meliorem finem." 10 quod] vt 0 quod ut v 13 mansuetissimel amantissime y 14 meis] tuis 'y custo- consolacione r 0 ego feci p feci Ab feci ego If Gh placebit melius y diunt p custodient n Gh te post vocaui dilectione Gh 15 captivam Ib a (ante delectacione) om. pi in] ad Gh te (post portum ipse) om. 17 duxit Y2 eduxit P Y1 0 Ab add.  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 15 81 Christus dicit sponse, quod prelati et litterati, qui de sciencia glorian- tur et ditantur et male viuunt, comparantur meretricibus et potatoribus vini. Qui se ipsos et alios in peccatis precipitant, cum tamen deberent esse magis virtuosi quam alii. Occurret tamen cum misericordia omni se conuertenti sicut pater exultans adepto filio. Cap. XV. "Ilie prelatus, pro quo tu oras, iam auertit oculos suos a me et vertit se ad mundum cum ornatu dignitatis sue. Si enim vellet esse meus, respiceret me cottidie, legeret librum meum attencius et non sic sollicite cogitaret in lege, que dicitur Ecclesie." 2 Cui illa respondit: "Numquid non, Domine mi, est lex tua lex Ecclesie?" Et Dominus respondit: "Lex mea erat, quamdiu mei legerunt eam et propter me legebatur. 3 Nunc autem non est mea, quia legitur iam in domo taxillatorum, qui tres punctos super vnum taxillum iaciunt; quia pro modica iusticia, quam in lege Ecclesie inueniunt, magnam summam pecunie acquirunt. 4 Nec legitur iam pro honore meo sed ad finem illum, quomodo pecunia acquiratur. In domo autem ludencium ad taxillos sunt meretrices, sunt potatores vini. 5 Tales nunc legunt legem meam, tales nunc nominantur scientes, sed vere sunt insi- pientes. Quid enim facere solet meretrix? Vtique solet esse procax in verbis, leuis in moribus, pulchra facie, ornata vestibus. 6 Tales sunt iam, qui legunt et addiscunt legem meam. Scurrilitas est in verbis eorum, numquam aperitur os eorum ad predicacionem meam, num- quam ad laudem meam. 7 Leues sunt in moribus, ita eciam quod seculares erubescunt de moribus eorum. Nec solum se ipsos precipi- tant, ymmo eciam alios secum exemplo suo trahunt. 8 Ipsi nichil affectant nisi videri a mundo et laudari honesti et honorati incedere vestibus suis, diuicias et honores acquirere. Verba mea et precepta sunt eis amara, vita et via mea est eis abhominabilis. 9 Vere conuer- sacio eorum et vita sic fetet in conspectu meo quasi meretrix. Quia sicut pre aliis mulieribus vilior et abieccior videtur meretrix, sic ipsi pre aliis sunt michi odiosi. 10 Dicunt enim et gloriantur se scire legem sed ad aliorum decepcionem et suam voluntatem.  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 17 85 Mater Dei docet sponsam, qualiter resistendo respondeat dyaboli suggestionibus cupiditatis et amicicie mundialium et luxurie, qualiter eciam anima, que est coniuncta Deo per caritatem, licet inquietetur per cogitaciones varias, si tamen resistit, non imputatur ei ad pecca- tum sed ad meritum et coronam. Cap. XVII. Maria loquebatur ad sponsam dicens: "Filia, si inimicus tuus blandi- tur tibi in delectacione bonorum temporalium, responde sibi: 'Ini- mice, tu nichil creasti, ideo nichil dare potes, et eciam si possis, cicius casura sunt et finitura.' 2 Si vero blanditur tibi in amicicia mundia- lium, dic sibi: 'Amicicia mundi finitur cum ve.' Si autem blanditur tibi cum voluptate carnis, responde sibi: 'Hanc nolo habere, quia in fine est quasi venenum et cum dolore terminatur.' 3 Tunc in ipso momento videbatur dyabolus, cui dixit beata virgo: "Dic ista audiente, vbi est, quod creasti?" Respondit demon: "Nichil ego creaui, quia creatura fui bona et a me ipso malus." 4 Tunc iterum beata virgo dixit: "Numquid aliquando amicicia tua terminum habuit felicem et cum gaudio?" Respondit demon: "Numquam fuit hoc et numquam erit." 5 Tercio ait beata virgo: "Responde et dic, numquid aliquando voluptas tua habuit bonum finem?" Et demon: "Numquam habuit bonum finem et numquam habebit, quia in malo incipit et ad malum tendit." 6 Tunc demon subiunxit ad virginem: "Tu virgo, da michi potesta- tem super istam!" Et virgo: "Quare non recipis eam in potestatem tuam?" 7 Et demon: "Non", inquit, "hoc possum, quia duplicem sanguinem in vno vase commixtum ego non possem separare et diuidere. Quia sanguis caritatis Dei est mixtus sanguini caritatis cordis eius." 8 Tunc iterum ait beata virgo: "Quare non permittis eam esse in sua quiete?" Respondit demon: "Hoc numquam faciam, quia, si non potero interficere eam per mortale peccatum, tunt XVII: 13 n Gh. §§ 9-10: cf. Ex. 57:8. Ideo promeruerunt sublimia. Et quomodo ista merebitur, que semper sentit sacietatem?" 14 Respondit iuuenis: "Christus docuit ieiunare, ne debilitetur corpus. Nec querit impossibilia nature sed moderan- ciam, nec querit, qualia et quanta quis sumit sed quali intencione sumit et caritate. 15 Quia consuetudo educacionis bone cum gracia- rum accione tenenda est, ne caro grauius infirmetur."  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 18 87 Christus dicit sponse, quod religiosi et alii spirituales recipientes con- solaciones Spiritus Sancti, qui non humiliter regraciantur Deo sed vilipendunt graciam et superbiunt ex ea et delectantes se in mundo attediantur de vita spirituali, assimilantur ingrato pauperi sicienti, qui, postquam gustat potum, proicit illum cum contumelia in oculos dato- ris. Cap. XVIII. "Quidam sunt quasi homo indigens et sitim paciens, cuius vocem paterfamilias audiens dat ei potum, quem habet optimum; accepto autem potu et gustato dicit: 2 'Non placet michi potus iste nec regracior tibi pro eo.' Et proicit potum in oculos datoris faciens ei contumeliam pro caritate. Accepta autem tali contumelia paterfami- lias, quia mitis est, cogitat apud se: 3 'Ecce hospes meus magnam iniuriam michi fecit, sed nolo me vindicare de illo, antequam ambo venerimus ad iudicem et tempus iudicii fuerit.' Et tunc abstergit a facie sua et fronte maculam et desiccat. 4 Sic faciunt nunc michi multi religiosi. Ipsi enim in paupertate sua et despeccione et contrarietate mundi clamant ad me et dicunt: 'Domine, vndique nobis despeccio et tribulacio; da nobis aliquam consolacionem!' 5 Tunc ego ex misericordia mea magna compacior eis et do eis vinum optimum, idest Spiritum Sanctum, cuius dulcedo replet animas eorum, cuius ardor non facit eos curare de despeccione et paupertate. 6 Gustato autem vino Spiritus mei et ad tempus habito vilipendunt hoc nec regraciantur michi. Et proiciunt illud in faciem meam, quando deliberant et optant magis esse cum mundo et quan- do ex gracia, quam habent, intumescunt. 7 Sic eciam ille michi nunc facit, quem tu nosti. Qui cum esset pauper et destitutus, consolabar eum Spiritu meo; cum esset despec- tus nec haberet anime exultacionem, ego fouebam eum gaudio meo. 8 Quia licet non quasi voce corporis loquar vel verba mea non aperte audiantur, tamen Spiritus meus in electis meis occulta inspiracione monet eos ad faciendum bona et incitat confortando ad meliora. 9 XVIII: p It Gh. Quia non solum pacienter suffero eum sed et pro ingratitudine rependo ei bona. 11 Nam maiorem nunc quam prius ab hominibus habet honorem et beniuolenciam et sufficiencius nunc solito impenduntur ei necessa- ria, sed ipse minus pro hiis quam prius deseruit michi. 12 Graciam c meam habet pro nichilo et dileccionem nullius reputacionis. Hec vt melius probes, satis ostendit tibi odor immutatus. 14 Quamdiu enim michi toto corde seruiuit et se ad me feruencius applicauit, flagrancia quedam suauis senciebatur in vestibus eius. Nec mirum, quia angeli virtute pleni amicos Dei circumdant cottidie et protegunt. 15 Nunc autem immutata voluntate immutatus est odor et talis odor nunc sentitur, qualis mentis est intencio et voluntas. 16 Quid autem ego facturus sum, cum potus meus in faciem meam proicitur?  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 19 89 Christus conqueritur de hominibus, qui delectantur in temporalibus deliciis despicientes futuram gloriam et beneficia passionis eius. Quo- rum oracio assimilatur voci canne et voci collisorum lapidum et tales dampnabuntur. Et tunc videbunt gloriam Dei intra celum et supra et infra et extra et in omni loco ad confusionem suam. Cap. XIX. "Ilie, quem tu nosti, cantat: 'Eripe me, Domine, ab homine malo!' Hec vox est in auribus meis quasi vox de fistula et quasi [vox] sonus canne. Vox labiorum eius est quasi sonus duorum lapidum colliso- rum. 2 Quis poterit respondere ad sonitum eius, cum, quid figurat, ignoratur? Eius enim cor quasi cum tribus vocibus clamat ad me. Prima dicit: 3 'Ego volo habere voluntatem meam, dormiam et surgam, cum michi placet. Verba placita erunt in labiis meis. Quod delectat et dulce est, intrabit in os meum. 4 Parsimoniam habere non curo sed quero sacietatem nature, et quod appetit, sufficienter dabo ei. Pecuniam desidero in bursa, molliciem vestium in dorso. Cum hec habuero, tunc habeo gaudium meum et quod desidero; hoc enim reputo felicitatem.' 5 Secunda vox eius clamat et dicit: 'Mors non est sic dura, vt dicitur, iudicium non est tam seuerum, vt scribitur. 6 Minantur enim predicatores plura et duriora propter cautelam sed reddentur minora propter misericordiam. Ideo, si habeo voluntatem meam in presenti, delectabile est michi et optimum; anima autem vadat, vbi possit.' 7 Tercia autem vox clamat et dicit: 'Deus non me creasset, nisi vellet michi dare celeste regnum; non passus fuisset, nisi vellet introducere me in patriam. 8 Et quare tam amaram penam pati voluit? Quis compulit eum aut que inde vtilitas? Quomodo scire possim celeste regnum? Non intelligo nisi ex quodam auditu. 9 1 Eripe me. . .malo Ps. 139,2 XIX: p t Gh. Cf. Rev. V reu. 8.  LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 19 91 Tercio omnia interiora mea et membra contremuerunt in passione. Sic steti ante eos et talia passus sum pro eis, sed hec omnia contemp- nunt, hec omnia negligunt sicut filius negligens matrem suam. 20 Numquid ego sicut mater fui eis? Que habens in vtero filium optat in hora partus, vt procedat infans viuus de vtero; si consequitur baptis- rna, non curat de morte sua. 21 Sic ego feci homini. Ego quasi mater peperi hominem de tenebris inferni passione mea ad diem perpe- tuum. Ego portaui eum quasi in vtero cum magna difficultate, cum omnia, que prophetata erant, compleui. 22 Ego paui eum cum lacte meo, cum verba bona ostendi et vite precepta dedi, sed ipse homo sicut malus filius negligens dolorem matris contempnit me pro cari- tate et exasperat, 23 facit michi pro dolore vteri ploratum, superad- dit vulneribus meis infirmitatem, porrigit michi pro esurie lapides, pro siti saciat me luto. 24 Quis autem est dolor iste, quem facit michi homo, cum imper- turbabilis et impassibilis sim in eternum manens Deus? Vere tunc facit michi homo quasi dolorem, quando se per peccatum separat a me, non quod aliquis dolor in me cadere possit, sed sicut alius pro alterius casu dolere solet. 25 Faciebat autem homo tunc michi dolo- rem, quando nesciebat, quid erat peccatum et quam graue, quando non habuit prophetas nec legem nec adhuc audierat verba oris mei. 26 Nunc autem facit michi super dolorem quasi quendam ploratum, licet immutabilis sim, quando cognita caritate mea et voluntate mea facit contra mandata mea et audacter peccat contra racionem con- sciencie sue. 27 Ex quo nunc profundius descendunt in infernum per cognicionem voluntatis mee, quam si mandata non optinuissent. Faciebat eciam michi homo quasi quedam vulnera, licet ego Deus vulnerari non possem, quando peccatum super peccatum addebat. 28 Nunc autem super vulnera mea quasi quandam addunt infirmitatem nocivam, cum non solum multiplicant peccata sed et gloriantur et 25 verba oris mei cfr Deut. 32,1 27 peccatum super peccatum Eccli. 5,5 24 autem est p 22 bona] mea Y r sicut] quasi P q Gh 20 et ante si add. Declaracio. 16 Hic fuit cognatus domine Birgitte et multum mundanus. Ammoni- cione diuina compunctus et conuersus est. Qui solitus erat dicere: "Quamdiu", inquit, "abhorrui penitencias, sensi me grauatum quasi pondere cathenarum. 17 Postquam frequentare cepi confessiones, sencio me sic alleuiatum et paratum in animo, quod nec attendo ad honores nec ad dampna domus, et nichil est michi dulce nisi loqui et audire de Deo." 18 Hic susceptis sacramentis Dei et in ore habens: "Ihesu dulcis, miserere mei!" obdormiuit in Domino. Propter preces tamen virginis alleuiatur pena eius. Cap. XXI. Maria loquitur: "Benedictum sit nomen tuum, fili mi!  96 B LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 21 2 Corpus tuum michi carissimum, quod in ventre meo generabatur et nutriebatur sine peccato, hodie pro anima istius defuncti consecra- tum est. Rogo igitur te, fili carissime, vt prosit anime eius, et miserere ei!" 3 Respondit Filius: "Benedicta sis tu, mater benedicta, ab omni creatura, quia misericordia tua innumerabilis est. Ego sum simflis homini, qui emit paruulum agrum quasi quinque pedum pro maximo precio, in quo aurum optimum erat absconditum. 4 Hic ager homo iste est quinque sensuum, quem preciosissimo sanguine meo compa- raui et redemi. In quo erat aurum preciosum, idest anima de deitate mea creata, que nunc a corpore sublata est et terra sola remanet. 5 Eius successores sunt similes homini potenti, qui vadens ad iudicium clamat lictori: 'Separa cum gladio caput eius a corpore eius! Non permittas eum diu viuere nec parcas sanguini eius!' 6 Sic faciunt illi. Ipsi enim quasi ad iudicium vadunt, cum pro salute anime patris decenter laborant, sed lictori clamant: 'Separa caput eius a corpore!' 7 Quis est iste lictor nisi dyabolus, separans animam consencientem sibi a Deo suo? Huic clamant: 'Separa!', quando contempta humili- tate illa bona, que agunt, faciunt pro superbia et honore mundi plus quam ex diuina caritate. 8 Per superbiam enim caput, idest Deus, separatur ab homine et coniungitur ei per humilitatem. Ipsi eciam clamant non diu viuere, quando non curant de morte eius, vt opti- neant bona. 9 Clamant et non parcere sanguini, quando non curant de amara pena eius nec quamdiu in ea fuerit, si voluntatem suam perficere possint. Eorum quippe cogitacio tota est ad mundum et pro modico est eis passlo mea." 10 Tunc respondit virgo: "Vidi iusticiam tuam, fili mi, seueram. Ad quam non loquor sed ad misericordiam tuam piissimam. Ideo propter preces meas miserere isti, quia cottidie legebat horas meas in honore meo. 11 Nec imputes ei superbiam successorum eius, quam pro eo exercent. Ipsi enim gaudent et iste plorat et punitur inconso- labiliter." 3 homini. . .absconditum cfr Matth. 13,44 clamat separata y eal eo y 2 nutriebar Gh clamant Abe clamat 0 Abl 7 Huic igitur] ergo Ab v q 9 idest ante quando add.  97 LIBRI SEXTI CAP. 21-22 12 Cui respondit Filius: "Benedicta sis tu, mater carissima! Verba c tua plena sunt dulcedine et dulciora melle, verba tua procedunt de corde, quod misericordia plenum est, et ideo misericordiam sonant verba tua. 13 Iste, pro quo tu oras, triplicem misericordiam propter te habebit. Primo saluabitur de manibus demonum, qui tamquam corui insaciabiliter affligunt eum. 14 Sicut enim aues, cum aliquem terribilem sonum audiunt, predam, quam vnguibus tenent, pre ti- more sonitus relinquunt et fugiunt, sic propter te demones relinquent animam eius nec vlterius tangent aut infestabunt. 15 Secundo trans- feretur de grauiori ardore in leuiorem. Tercio consolabuntur eum angeli sancti. Adhuc tamen ex toto non est liberatus et adhuc auxilio indiget. 16 Scis enim et vides omnem iusticiam in me, quod nullus ad beatitudinem ingredi potest, nisi tamquam aurum per ignem purga- tum mundatus fuerit. Ideo propter preces tuas adueniente tempore misericordie et iusticie liberabitur ex toto." Christus recipit ad misericordiam precibus matris sue quendam epis- copum nudum bonis operibus sed nouiter conuersum ad contricionem et bonum et sanctum propositum vite.
